It is crucial to sanitize and validate any environment variables before use.\n\n2. **Buffer Overflow Risks**:\n   - The use of `memcpy` without checking the size of the destination buffer (lines 108, 111, 114, 120, 123) can lead to buffer overflows. This is a significant vulnerability as it can allow an attacker to overwrite memory, potentially leading to arbitrary code execution (CWE-120). The code should ensure that the destination buffer is large enough to hold the data being copied.\n\n3. **Dynamic Memory Allocation**:\n   - The code uses `xmalloc0` and `xstrdup` for dynamic memory allocation. Proper error handling should be implemented to check if the memory allocation was successful.\n\n4. **Socket Usage**:\n   - The use of `socket` (lines 24) indicates a network connection, which can introduce vulnerabilities if not properly secured.
